Timestamp: 2015-06-01 08:55:09
Where were you?: NE 57th Ave and NE Sacramento Street
When did this occur?: 2015-04-07 08:00:00
What happened?: In early April, the City made a change to NE 57th Ave at the intersection with NE Sacramento St. There is now a painted median in the middle of NE 57th, with bike lanes and auto lanes angling to the right. While cars driving this route have quickly caught onto the street change, many cars are still being parked along the curbs in what is now the bike lane. This creates a dangerous pinch point for cyclists attempting to use the bike lanes, particularly in heavy traffic during commuting hours. Bikes are forced to take the lane or come to an unplanned stop, often while moving quickly downhill (when headed south). I suspect that part of the issue for parking cars is that they don't realize they are now parking in a bike lane, when 2 weeks earlier the same location was a legal parking spot. On April 8 I requested that the City take action to complete this street modification by adding "No Parking" signs and paint where the bike lane is directly beside the curb, and then by enforcing the no parking areas. The City responded to my email with a "we'll get back to you in 12 weeks" email. They also put up some temporary "no parking" signs, but only prohibiting parking 7 am to 6 pm. And these were often ignored. Perhaps when a crew was out there working something was actually done. It took approximately 6 weeks for the city to (mostly) stripe the reconfigured bike lane with something more than spraypaint. No work has been done in this intersection in recent weeks, but the temporary no parking signs are gone, and the no parking areas have not been modified to correspond with the bike lanes. I'm not sure what the City's specific intent is with this intersection. My assumption is that it is meant to improve crossing safety for pedestrians attempting to cross NE 57th (despite the presence of a signaled crosswalk 1/2 block further south). Since the lane configuration change, I have observed many more cars stopping for pedestrians at this intersection. If that is the intent, here is some anecdotal evidence that it's working. As things are currently configured, however, the potential safety improvement for pedestrians is far outweighed by the risk to cyclists. I use this intersection as a cyclist, pedestrian, and driver, and the work at this intersection needs to be completed quickly. I hope something can be done quickly and before someone is injured at this intersection. I have had three near-misses here, that required me braking suddenly or swerving out of the way of a moving or illegally parked vehicle. I am cautious enough of the known danger to go slowly and with care, now that I've been at risk.
Do you believe the driver committed a traffic violation?: The driver broke a traffic law
What best describes the situation?: Vehicle blocking bike lane, Lack of safe infrastructure, Excessive speed

I suppose it's somewhat comforting to know that not everybody is out to hurt me for the mere act of riding a bike.

Timestamp: 2015-06-11 15:06:07
Where were you?: NW Naito and Steel Bridge (waterfront path)
When did this occur?: 2015-06-11 09:30:00
What happened?: From: Scott Kocher Sent: Thursday, June 11, 2015 3:03 PM To: novick@portlandoregon.gov; Amanda@portlandoregon.gov Cc: PDOT Traffic Safety and Livability (safe@portlandoregon.gov); Aptekar, Bryan (Bryan.Aptekar@portlandoregon.gov) Subject: Waterfront near miss Dear Commissioners Fritz and Novick: This morning I was riding my bicycle to work on the path in the Esplanade a few yards south of the Steel Bridge. I was wearing hi viz, with a front light on full strobe, in dry daylight conditions, when I was nearly struck head-on by an orange City of Portland forklift being operated in the path. I was not traveling fast, and I saw when she came from the grass onto the path and started coming at me. I stopped. I screamed. She looked where she was going just in time to stop. Everyone was ok, this time, but it was a very dangerous and unwelcome situation. This path is possibly the most heavily-used path in Oregon for people of all ages to bike, walk, and run. The City (Parks?) has vehicles on the path to facilitate festivals, and on a daily basis emptying trash cans, etc. I hope City employees operating vehicles on the path will be extremely careful in this environment. Hoping that people will be careful, however, doesn’t solve a dangerous environment. May I suggest: FLAGGERS It would be helpful to have standard work zone precautions, such as flaggers and cones, any time the path is being used as a work zone. This morning there was nobody helping the forklift operator, and no cones or markers for the work zone. A SAFE PLACE TO RIDE AND WALK ALONG NAITO Big picture, the waterfront path is overcrowded. I would prefer not to ride a bike there. But, there is no connection for my route–Naito north of the Steel Bridge to downtown–without going onto the path. Staying on Naito under the Steel Bridge means negotiating multiple shallow-angle railroad tracks (where I have seen bicycle crashes), and narrow bridge footings with fast traffic and no place to ride a bicycle for several blocks. The only path under the bridge that is not currently in use as an encampment is the one I was on. As a daily user for most of the last fourteen years, I increasingly see collisions, near misses, and uncomfortable and unsafe encounters with people who are intoxicated or impaired along the waterfront path, particularly around the Steel, Burnside and Morrison bridges downtown. I hope soon we will have a safe place to ride, run, and walk along Naito that connects to the Hawthorne and Steel Bridges, and Naito north of the Steel Bridge, as a viable alternative to the overcrowded and currently out-of-control waterfront path. Thank you for your work to provide immediate and longer-term solutions. Scott Scott F. Kocher │ Attorney at Law Tel: 503.445.2102 │ Fax: 503.445.2120 811 SW Naito Parkway, Suite 420 │ Portland, OR 97204 scott@forumlawgroup.com │ www.forumlawgroup.com
Do you believe the driver committed a traffic violation?: The driver broke a traffic law
What best describes the situation?: Lack of safe infrastructure, Inattentive driver, unsafe work zone

Timestamp: 2015-09-22 19:43:19
Where were you?: SE 43rd Ave and SE Clinton St.
When did this occur?: 2015-09-22 18:25:00
What happened?: I was biking eastbound on SE Clinton. Two cars were driving in my lane to pass some cyclists on the hill. This was nearly a head-on collision. Because it was two cars together, it either would have been a pile-up or two cars running right over me. ORS 811.410(1)(c) states: The driver of a vehicle shall not drive to the left side of the center of the roadway in overtaking and passing a vehicle proceeding in the same direction unless the left side is **clearly visible** and is free of oncoming traffic for a sufficient distance ahead to permit the overtaking and passing to be completed without interfering with the operation of a vehicle approaching from the opposite direction or a vehicle overtaken. There is a hill on Clinton between 45th Ave and 43rd. This hill makes it impossible for a driver to determine whether the left-hand side is free of oncoming traffic, as required by ORS 811.410(1)(c). Even if I was not coming in the other direction, it *still* would have been illegal for those drivers to pass those bikes there.
Do you believe the driver committed a traffic violation?: The driver broke a traffic law
What best describes the situation?: Passing without sufficient space, Wrong side of road

Where were you?: NW St Helens Rd and NW Doane Ave, Portland, OR
When did this occur?: 2015-12-18 10:30:00
What happened?: I was riding WB in the bicycle lane of Hwy 30. Two large trucks passed me just as the bicycle lane narrowed to approximately 2 feet. It is scary and unsafe. I emailed ODOT: From: Scott Kocher Sent: Friday, December 18, 2015 3:37 PM To: Ask ODOT (Ask.ODOT@odot.state.or.us) Cc: roger.geller@portlandoregon.gov Subject: NW St Helens Rd bike lane gaps Dear ODOT: Would you please address the following two gaps in the west-bound bicycle lane of NW St Helens Rd (aka Hwy 30) in Northwest Portland? 1. The maintained asphalt of the WB bike lane narrows to about two feet at the intersection with NW Doane Avenue. There is no obstruction or other apparent reason why the full width of asphalt is not maintained. A picture (looking west) is attached. The narrowing creates a hazard for people using the bicycle lane, including people who must walk there because there is no sidewalk, and also affects access to the TriMet bus stop at this location. As pictured, heavy truck traffic and high speeds make the situation unsafe here. 2. A few hundred yards to the west, at 6589 NW St Helens Rd, gravel accumulates semi-permanently in the bike lane. See photo attached, and BikePortland article from two years ago which discusses this problem at this location and includes photos of it, as well: http://bikeportland.org/2014/01/24/lack-of-sweeping-makes-for-challenging-conditions-on-dirty-30-100154 The curve reduces sight distance at this location where people riding bicycles and walking are put into traffic to avoid the gravel and long-term standing water. In the past I have talked with Region 1 maintenance about this issue. I was told that ODOT will not consider asphalt “skirts” or bibs at the property entrances or increasing the frequency of sweeps (currently perhaps 3 to 4 times per year) to address the gravel. I was told ODOT will not address the drainage problem because there may be underground utilities in the area. Pooling water (see picture attached) which typically remains from October through June. The attached Portland Bikeways map shows these two locations. I have marked them in red. As you likely know, on Saturday a person was killed at a bike lane gap on Highway 30B (aka NE Lombard St), 11 miles east of these locations. That tragedy raised discussion about whether ODOT is “aware” of bike lane gaps for purposes of budgeting or planning. The two gaps I have described appear to be a maintenance problem, not something that should require budgeting or planning. To the extent any budgeting or planning is needed, however, please communicate this information to the people within ODOT who may need to be aware. I would be grateful to know what response is planned for these two locations. If for any reason solving these problems is not going to happen right away please ensure that ODOT and Portland Bureau of Transportation staff who are responsible for updating bikeway maps are aware that the bicycle lane currently mapped at these locations is not usable. Thank you, Scott Scott F. Kocher │ Attorney at Law Tel: 503.445.2102 │ Fax: 503.445.2120 811 SW Naito Parkway, Suite 420 │ Portland, OR 97204 scott@forumlawgroup.com │ www.forumlawgroup.com

As I crossed the southbound lane of SE 20th and began to enter the cut in the barrier that is intended to stop motor vehicles from going east or west on Harrison, I had to yell at the driver to stop. He stopped just as I was about to cross in front of him. He did not stop until he was more than a car length past the stop sign. I have ridden, walked, and driven through this intersection thousands of times. I have seen so many violations - from blatant running of the stop sign like today, to drivers who think it's ok to "piggyback" on the car that stopped ahead of them, to motorists who drive over the barrier. My fellow cyclists are just as guilty of blowing through the stop signs as motorists. Too often I see cyclists heading west on SE Harrison traveling at 20 MPH plus who blow through that stop sign even when there are cars already stopped on SE 20th. The Portland police need to do a sting here before someone is maimed or killed. In the 26 years I've been traveling through this intersection, this is at least the third time that I could have been seriously injured, or worse, while riding my bike.

Timestamp: 2019-06-26 00:29:46
Where were you?: 5th Ave N and Roy St, Seattle, WA
When did this occur?: 2019-06-14 16:15:00
What happened?: The incident occurred on Friday, June 14th at approximately 4:15pm while I was commuting from my home to my workplace. The location of the incident was the intersection of 5th Ave N and Roy St in Seattle, WA. Visibility at the time of the incident was clear. I was traveling south on 5th Ave N where there are clear shared lane markings for bicycles, and after the intersection with Roy St, a dedicated bicycle lane. I travel this route safely multiple times every weekday to commute from my home to my office. I was in full control at the time of the incident and wearing a full-face helmet. I approached the intersection while the light was already green for my direction with the intention to travel straight across towards Mercer St. Floro was traveling north on 5th Ave N and intended to make a left turn from 5th Ave N onto Roy St, across my path of travel. The left turn onto Roy St. from 5th Ave N is arrow-controlled, has a clearly-marked sign saying "LEFT TURN YIELD ON GREEN" and flashes a yellow caution arrow while the opposite direction is green. I had already entered the intersection on a green light and was traveling straight across when Floro entered the intersection. Floro failed to yield as instructed by the multiple markings, and accelerated to turn sharply left onto Roy St, directly into my path of travel. As soon as I saw Floro's vehicle accelerating directly towards me, I engaged the brakes as hard as possible and put my arms up in an attempt to protect my body. Floro continued to accelerate directly into me and struck my full body with the front right of his vehicle. I lost consciousness for several seconds after being struck by Floro's vehicle and was flung backwards onto the pavement. After I regained consciousness, a female bystander who had witnessed the accident ran up to me in the middle of the intersection, asked me if I was okay and mentioned that Floro was staring at her on the corner of the intersection while he accelerated into me. Floro continued to drive onto Roy St. After several moments, I was able to stand up, gather some of my belongings and limp out of the intersection in pain to find Floro on Roy St where I called 911 and we exchanged information.
Do you believe the driver committed a traffic violation?: The driver broke a traffic law
What best describes the situation?: Left-hook (oncoming driver at intersection turns in front of cyclist's path), Inattentive driver
